< Review>
The show we saw "White" was amazing, with a great set design and great cast. The show was biting, witty and made you think. There was a nice mini discussion with patrons after which I wish I had more of when going to shows.
Also nice little area for food/drinks with sweet staff.
Cute raffle that apparently happens with each show.
Check online for MAD and other pay-what-you-can offers if you need to be frugal.

Saw the play Arcadia. 'Twas a creative and clever performance across time. If you're one for philosophy and/or debate I would highly recommend going to watch.

The performance hall itself was fairly cozy. Seats were reasonably comfortable and positioned 360 degrees about the stage (but with most on a single side). Lighting was on point throughout the show, hats off to not only the actors but the directors and stage hands.</text>

Shotgun Players offers an alternative approach, more focused on creativity and innovation, with a bit less focus on popular, commercial theatre.  I went to a reading of The Cherry Orchard recently, and have seen several other shows in the past.  Parking isn't always convenient, so consider taking the BART to get there. <review>Great local theater across the street form Ashby BART. I saw the troupe perform William S. Gibbons "The Black Rider", featuring music from Tom Waits. The band was exceptional; I'm a huge fan of mid-career Waits, and the band captured his junk-symphony vibe to a T. I'm not particularly knowledgeable about acting, so I can't comment on the skill of the actors, they clearly were having a good time performing the show (for what it's worth, I saw one of the last showings of an extended run, a time when I can easily see the actors tiring of their roles, but that was not noticeable with the Shotgun Players). I had a seat in the back corner, which wouldn't seem ideal (it was one of the last to go), but visibility and comfort we're not issues. There is a bar and you can enjoy your cocktail inside the theater. Recommended! I will be returning.</review>< pictures>

< Text>
What?  You haven't been to Shotgun Players yet?  You've driven by, you've noticed the way they repaint the building for every show, kinda wondered about it, but you just weren't sure whether to swerve away from the standards like Berkeley Rep.  Go ahead and swerve, my friend - right into the BART parking lot across the street (or better yet, just take BART there), and you will treat yourself to some of the best theatre the Bay Area has to offer. This is intelligent, thought-provoking, talk about it afterward, wow, that was really something kind of an evening, with extraordinary actors - some you'll recognize, some up and coming.  Subscribe for a really good deal (check out the WOW deal), or the under 30's deal, or the nights that are pay what you wish, or check out their Champagne Reading Series - just $15 a pop.
We've subscribed for the past 5 years, but I grieve all the years before that I could have been here!  Don't make the same mistake, check it out!</Text>

<user>108778722137963556739< /user><user_name>Ryan O'Connor</user_name><Time>1452463308719<//Time><rate>2< /rate>< Text>
We've had good experiences here in the 3 previous times we went here. Today we had my 5 year old twins' birthday party at Get Air. Nicole, at the front desk, said the smaller kids could jump in the big area unless it got too busy, which has been standard in our experience.

But then I met Evan who told me in an incredibly condescending manner, that the smaller kids would not be allowed to jump in the big area at all, regardless of how busy it was. I pointed out that there were 6.kids jumping at that moment plus my two, but Evan insisted that 6 kids constituted "busy" and ushered my kids to the small area. I told him that it was ridiculous that my kids, who were part of an expensive party, could not jump. He then told me that if I were to continue to argue with him he would write an incident report. What?!? He explained that he was in charge and it was too bad if I didn't like his decision.

I ended up speaking with Gavin, who was also on the floor. He was at that point unaware of my conversation with Evan. He said as long as it wasn't busy, there weren't a lot of bigger kids jumping, and he was comfortable with the safety of my kids they could stay in the big area. He was very friendly.

My kids spent the next hour and a half jumping in the big area. Gavin was incredibly friendly. Nicole was the hostess for the party and was great with the kids. Gavin and Nicole helped make it a nice day for my kids and their friends.

Evan, on the other hand, seemed to spend a lot of time staring at me. Several times he winked at me. From my perspective, this was simply antagonizing and certainly inappropriate I'm addition to the threat of an "incident report". I cannot understand how someone who acts like Evan did would or should be employed in a place where kids visit.

Overall, I would recommend having a birthday party at Get Air. But I hope that the management takes a look at how Evan acts.<//Text>

My girlfriend and I have lived at Portola Court for a little over a year now and love it! We love it so much we decided to transfer to a larger floor plan and commit to another year. The community is very quiet and well built. I am a heavy walker, and as far as I know have never had it be an issue for anyone below us. We also never hear any of our neighbors. As far as apartments go, this is pretty rare. At most communities you can hear your neighbors thumping around. We also appreciate that some of the three story buildings have elevators, which many communities reserve for the 4 story+ buildings, and that each home comes with a detached garage (built in shelving included).

Donald the community manager, and Sean the assistant manager have made our transfer process painless. They have both truly gone above and beyond to ensure we will be happy in our new home. I can be a pain in the butt sometimes, but they have never let their service falter. It is obvious that they both care about the happiness of their residents and take pride in their community.

We are looking forward to another year here, and would highly recommend anyone looking for a quiet community away from the bustle of the Spectrum area to check out Portola Court.<//text>
